Aref Abdul Razzik of [Tayibe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tayibe "Tayibe") was responsible for the area south of Tulkarm and was known for evading capture whilst being pursued by the security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228–230_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228%E2%80%93230-193">[186]</a></sup> He signed his bulletins as 'The Ghost of Sheikh Qassam'.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228–230_193-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228%E2%80%93230-193">[186]</a></sup> Razzik assumed a place in British army folklore and the troops sang a song about him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228–230_193-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228%E2%80%93230-193">[186]</a></sup> Razzik was capable and daring and gained a reputation as one of the army's problem heroes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228–230_193-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_228%E2%80%93230-193">[186]</a></sup>

#### Jerusalem area

[Issa Battat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Issa_Battat "Issa Battat") was a peasant leader in the southern hills below Jerusalem who caused enormous damage to security patrols in his area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_235,_238_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_235,_238-194">[187]</a></sup> He was killed by a patrol of armed police in a battle near Hebron in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_235,_238_194-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne2003225,_235,_238-194">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-195">[188]</a></sup>

#### Arab volunteers

In the first phase of the revolt, around 300 volunteers, mostly veterans of the [Ottoman Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Army "Ottoman Army") and/or rebels from the [Great Syrian Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Syrian_Revolt "Great Syrian Revolt") (1925–27), deployed in northern Palestine. Their overall commander was Fawzi al-Qawuqji and his deputies were [Said al-As](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Said_al-As "Said al-As") and [Muhammad al-Ashmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_al-Ashmar "Muhammad al-Ashmar"). Qawuqji also led the volunteer force's Iraqi and Transjordanian battalions, and al-Ashmar was commander of the Syrian battalion, which largely consisted of volunteers from Damascus's [al-Midan Quarter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Midan "Al-Midan"), [Hama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hama "Hama") and [Homs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homs "Homs"). The Druze ex-Ottoman officer, [Hamad Sa'ab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamad_Sa%27ab "Hamad Sa'ab"), commanded the [Lebanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_people "Lebanese people") battalion.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

### Funding

In the contest of wills between the British Empire and Palestinian aspirants for statehood, the respective efforts to secure the financial means to sustain the hostilities also played out as a battle for funding.<sup id="cite_ref-196"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-196">[h]</a></sup> The Mandatory Authority's repression of the revolt was bankrolled directly from London and through the revenue stream supplied to the administration by land and property taxes, stamp duties, excises on manufactured goods and customs duties on imports and exports. Draconian [collective punishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_punishment "Collective punishment") fines on the peasantry –many heavily burdened already by debt and unable to pay them – were such that revenue extracted from punitive fines exceeded, and more than compensated for, the revenue lost during the revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes201983–87_197-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes201983%E2%80%9387-197">[189]</a></sup>

The majority of funds raised to finance the uprising came from Arab/Muslim sources. In the broader Arab/Muslim world a measure of financial aid, never vast, filtered in from Egypt, Syria, Iraq and Muslim India for some time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106_198-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106-198">[190]</a></sup> In Palestine, the peasantry, often debt-ridden, could offer little towards subsidising the resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes201983_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes201983-199">[191]</a></sup> A variety of measures were adopted. Women donated jewelry and ran fund-raising committees:, a [jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jihad "Jihad") tax was placed on citrus groves, the industry being the backbone of Palestine's export trade; Palestinians on the government payroll contributed sums anywhere up to half of their salaries; levies were imposed on wealthier Arabs (many of whom went abroad to avoid paying them, or because they could not meet demands to provide financial aid to strikers).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107,_110_200-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107,_110-200">[192]</a></sup> The AHC's functions in this capacity were truncated when it was abolished by the British authorities in October 1937. Displaced in Damascus, its leaders were cut off from contact with field units and donations gradually dried up.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes201980_201-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes201980-201">[193]</a></sup> al-Husayni, by then in exile, proved unable to raise money, and in Syria militant contacts were informed by July 1938 that they would have to make do on their own.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107_202-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107-202">[194]</a></sup> By 1938 the drop in revenues caused militant gangs to resort to extortion and robbery, often draining villages of ready cash reserves set aside to pay government fines, which then had to be met by the sale of crops and livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019109_203-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019109-203">[195]</a></sup> Some contributions were obtained from American sources.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107_202-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019107-202">[194]</a></sup>

A great deal of speculation later arose around the purported role of Germany and Italy in backing the revolt financially, based on early claims by Jewish operatives that both countries were fomenting the uprising by funneling cash and weapons to the insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-206"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-206">[i]</a></sup> German plans to ship arms to the rebels were never implemented due to distrust of the Saudi middlemen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364-207">[198]</a></sup> Italian attempts to furnish arms by the same venue were thwarted by British intelligence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106_198-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106-198">[190]</a></sup> The British never found arms or munitions of German or Italian provenance. RAF intelligence dismissed these claims as either referring to ‘comparatively small’ sums or as purveyed to bring discredit on the Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019103,_106_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019103,_106-208">[199]</a></sup> al-Husayni and his associates received limited<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes201987_209-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes201987-209">[200]</a></sup> funding from [Fascist Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist_Italy_(1922%E2%80%931943) "Fascist Italy (1922–1943)") during the revolt as the Italians were in dispute with the United Kingdom over [Abyssinia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire "Ethiopian Empire") and wished not only to disrupt the British rear<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999133_210-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999133-210">[201]</a></sup> but also to extend Italian influence in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArielli2008187–204_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArielli2008187%E2%80%93204-211">[202]</a></sup> The rebels utilized the Italian funding to smuggle weapons into Palestine via Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia201486_212-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia201486-212">[203]</a></sup> Total Italian funding amounted to approximately £150.000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFiore201089_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFiore201089-213">[204]</a></sup> It stopped in late 1938<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106_198-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019106-198">[190]</a></sup> and played no decisive role since the uprising peaked after that date.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFiore2010109–110_214-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFiore2010109%E2%80%93110-214">[205]</a></sup>

In the first years after 1933 Germany was approached by a variety of Arab nationalist groups from Palestine and abroad asking for aid, but Germany categorically refused. Maintaining good relations with the British was still considered to be of the uppermost priority, hence it limited itself to expressing its sympathy and moral support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia201474–78_215-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia201474%E2%80%9378-215">[206]</a></sup> Soon after the outbreak of the revolt, in December 1936, Germany was approached by the rebel commander Fawzi al-Qawuqji and in January 1937 by representatives of the Arab Higher Committee, both requesting arms and money, but again in vain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia201481–82_216-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia201481%E2%80%9382-216">[207]</a></sup> In July al-Husayni himself approached [Heinrich Doehle](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Doehle "de:Heinrich Doehle"), new general counsel of Jerusalem, to request support for the "battle against the Jews".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerf200929–30_217-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerf200929%E2%80%9330-217">[208]</a></sup> Doehle found that Germany's hesitation in supporting the rebels had caused pro-German sentiment among Palestinian Arabs to waver.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerf200928–29,_30_218-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerf200928%E2%80%9329,_30-218">[209]</a></sup> Some limited<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-220">[j]</a></sup> German funding for the revolt can be dated to around the summer of 1938<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364_207-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364-207">[198]</a></sup> and was perhaps related to a goal of distracting the British from the on-going [occupation of Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Czechoslovakia_(1938%E2%80%931945) "Occupation of Czechoslovakia (1938–1945)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia2014108–109_221-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia2014108%E2%80%93109-221">[211]</a></sup> The [Abwehr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abwehr "Abwehr") gave money to al-Husayni<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364_207-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364-207">[198]</a></sup> and other sums were funneled via [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia2014109_222-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia2014109-222">[212]</a></sup>

## Outcome

### Casualties

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/WhitePaper1939riot.jpg/220px-WhitePaper1939riot.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:WhitePaper1939riot.jpg)

Jewish protest demonstration against the [Palestine White Paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939"), 18 May 1939

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/WhitePaper1939Poster.jpg/220px-WhitePaper1939Poster.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:WhitePaper1939Poster.jpg)

Jewish protest demonstrations against the 1939 Palestine White Paper. One of the big posters displayed the previous day.

Despite the intervention of up to 50,000 British troops and 15,000 Haganah men, the uprising continued for over three years. By the time it concluded in September 1939, more than 5,000 Arabs, over 300 Jews, and 262 Britons had been killed and at least 15,000 Arabs were wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a_1-27"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a-1">[1]</a></sup>

### Impact on the Jewish Yishuv

In the overall context of the Jewish settlement's development in the 1930s the physical losses endured during the revolt were relatively insignificant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> Although hundreds were killed and property was damaged no Jewish settlement was captured or destroyed and several dozen new ones were established.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> Over 50,000 new Jewish immigrants arrived in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> In 1936 Jews made up about one-third of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008295_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008295-223">[213]</a></sup>

The hostilities contributed to further disengagement of the Jewish and Arab economies in Palestine, which were intertwined to some extent until that time. Development of the economy and infrastructure accelerated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> For example, whereas the Jewish city of [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") relied on the nearby Arab seaport of [Jaffa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa "Jaffa"), hostilities dictated the construction of a separate Jewish-run seaport for Tel Aviv,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> inspiring the delighted Ben-Gurion to note in his diary "we ought to reward the Arabs for giving us the impetus for this great creation."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999388_224-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999388-224">[214]</a></sup> Metal works were established to produce armoured sheeting for vehicles and a rudimentary arms industry was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> The settlement's [transportation capabilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egged_(company) "Egged (company)") were enhanced and Jewish unemployment was relieved owing to the employment of police officers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160_31-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999160-31">[29]</a></sup> and replacement of striking Arab labourers, employees, craftsman and farmers by Jewish workers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008295_223-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008295-223">[213]</a></sup> Most of the important industries in Palestine were owned by Jews and in trade and the banking sector they were much better placed than the Arabs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008295_223-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008295-223">[213]</a></sup>

As a result of collaboration with the British colonial authorities and security forces many thousands of young men had their first experience of military training, which [Moshe Shertok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moshe_Sharett "Moshe Sharett") and Haganah leader [Eliyahu Golomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eliyahu_Golomb "Eliyahu Golomb") cited as one of the fruits of the [Haganah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haganah "Haganah")'s policy of [havlagah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Havlagah "Havlagah") (restraint).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShapira1999250_225-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShapira1999250-225">[215]</a></sup>

Although the Jewish settlement in Palestine was dismayed by the publication of the 1939 White Paper restricting Jewish immigration, David Ben-Gurion remained undeterred, believing that the policy would not be implemented, and in fact Neville Chamberlain had told him that the policy would last at the very most only for the duration of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999449_226-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999449-226">[216]</a></sup> In the event the White Paper quotas were exhausted only in December 1944, over five and a half years later, and in the same period the United Kingdom absorbed 50,000 Jewish refugees and the British Commonwealth (Australia, Canada and South Africa) took many thousands more.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999439,_459_227-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999439,_459-227">[217]</a></sup> During the War over 30,000 Jews joined the British forces and even the Irgun ceased operations against the British until 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999450–451_228-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999450%E2%80%93451-228">[218]</a></sup>

### Impact on the Palestinian Arabs

The revolt weakened the military strength of Palestinian Arabs in advance of their ultimate confrontation with the Jewish settlement in the [1947–48 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%9348_Civil_War_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–48 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine") and was, according to [Benny Morris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Morris "Benny Morris"), thus counterproductive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999121_229-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999121-229">[219]</a></sup> During the uprising, British authorities attempted to confiscate all weapons from the Arab population. This, and the destruction of the main Arab political leadership in the revolt, greatly hindered their military efforts in the [1948 Palestine war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestine_war "1948 Palestine war"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159_32-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159-32">[30]</a></sup> where imbalances between the Jewish and Arab economic performance, social cohesion, political organisation and military capability became apparent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008295_223-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008295-223">[213]</a></sup>

The Mufti, Hajj Amin al-Husseini and his supporters directed a Jihad against any person who did not obey the Mufti. Their national struggle was a religious holy war, and the incarnation of both the Palestinian Arab nation and Islam was Hajj Amin al-Husseini. Anyone who rejected his leadership was a heretic and his life was forfeit.<sup id="cite_ref-231"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-231">[k]</a></sup> After the Peel report publication, the murders of Arabs leaders who opposed the Mufti were accelerated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2009122_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2009122-232">[221]</a></sup> Pressed by the assassination campaign pursued by the rebels at the behest of the Husseini leadership, the opposition had a security cooperation with the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2009146_170-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2009146-170">[164]</a></sup> The flight of wealthy Arabs, which occurred during the revolt, was also replicated in 1947–49.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008291_85-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008291-85">[82]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/LondonConference1939.jpg/220px-LondonConference1939.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LondonConference1939.jpg)

[London Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Conference_(1939) "London Conference (1939)"), St. James' Palace, February 1939. Palestinian delegates (foreground), left to right: Fu'ad Saba, Yaqub Al-Ghussein, [Musa Alami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musa_Alami "Musa Alami"), Amin Tamimi, [Jamal Al-Husseini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamal_Al-Husseini "Jamal Al-Husseini"), [Awni Abdul Hadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awni_Abdul_Hadi "Awni Abdul Hadi"), [George Antonious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Antonious "George Antonious"), and Alfred Roch. Facing are the British, with [Neville Chamberlain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain") presiding. To his right is [Lord Halifax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Wood,_1st_Earl_of_Halifax "Edward Wood, 1st Earl of Halifax"), and to his left, [Malcolm MacDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malcolm_MacDonald "Malcolm MacDonald").

Thousands of Palestinian houses were destroyed, and massive financial costs were incurred because of the general strike and the devastation of fields, crops and orchards. The economic boycott further damaged the fragile Palestinian Arab economy through loss of sales and goods and increased unemployment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159–160_233-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159%E2%80%93160-233">[222]</a></sup> The revolt did not achieve its goals, although it is "credited with signifying the birth of the Arab Palestinian identity."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENashif200824_234-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENashif200824-234">[223]</a></sup> It is generally credited with forcing the issuance of the [White Paper of 1939](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939") in which Britain retreated from the partition arrangements proposed by the Peel Commission in favour of the creation of a [binational state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-state_solution "One-state solution") within ten years, although The League of Nations commission held that the White Paper was in conflict with the terms of the Mandate as put forth in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-avalon_111-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-avalon-111">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-235">[l]</a></sup> The [White Paper of 1939](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939") was regarded by many as incompatible with the commitment to a Jewish National Home in Palestine, as proclaimed in the 1917 [Balfour Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration "Balfour Declaration"). Al-Husseini rejected the new policy, although it seems that the ordinary Palestinian Arab accepted the [White Paper of 1939](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939"). His biographer, [Philip Mattar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_Mattar "Philip Mattar") wrote that in that case, the Mufti preferred his personal interests and the ideology rather than the practical considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159_32-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999159-32">[30]</a></sup>

### Impact on the British Empire

As the inevitable war with [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") approached, British policy makers concluded that although they could rely on the support of the Jewish population in Palestine, who had no alternative but to support Britain, the support of Arab governments and populations in an area of great strategic importance for the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") was not assured.<sup id="cite_ref-segev437_236-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-segev437-236">[224]</a></sup> Prime Minister [Neville Chamberlain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain") concluded "if we must offend one side, let us offend the Jews rather than the Arabs."<sup id="cite_ref-segev437_236-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-segev437-236">[224]</a></sup>

In February 1939 Secretary of State for Dominion Affairs [Malcolm MacDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malcolm_MacDonald "Malcolm MacDonald") called together a conference of Arab and Zionist leaders on the future of Palestine at [St. James's Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._James%27s_Palace "St. James's Palace") in London but the discussions ended without agreement on 27 March.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrämer2008293_141-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr%C3%A4mer2008293-141">[135]</a></sup>The government's new policy as published in White Paper of 17 May had been determined already and despite Jewish protests and Irgun attacks the British remained resolute.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999437_237-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999437-237">[225]</a></sup>

There was a growing feeling among British officials that there was nothing left for them to do in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999437_237-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999437-237">[225]</a></sup> Perhaps the ultimate achievement of the Arab Revolt was to make the British sick of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999443_238-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999443-238">[226]</a></sup> Major-General Bernard "Monty" Montgomery concluded, "the Jew murders the Arab and the Arab murders the Jew. This is what is going on in Palestine now. And it will go on for the next 50 years in all probability."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999442_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999442-239">[227]</a></sup>

## Historiography

The 1936–39 Arab Revolt has been and still is marginalized in both Western and [Israeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") historiography on Palestine, and even progressive Western scholars have little to say about the [anti-colonial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-imperialism "Anti-imperialism") struggle of the Palestinian Arab rebels against the British Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003xxii,_13–15_240-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003xxii,_13%E2%80%9315-240">[228]</a></sup> According to Swedenburg's analysis, for instance, the Zionist version of Israeli history acknowledges only one authentic national movement: the struggle for Jewish [self-determination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination "Self-determination") that resulted in the [Israeli Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence "Israeli Declaration of Independence") in May 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003xxii,_13–15_240-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003xxii,_13%E2%80%9315-240">[228]</a></sup> Swedenburg writes that the Zionist narrative has no room for an anticolonial and anti-British Palestinian national revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003?_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003?-241">[229]</a></sup> Zionists often describe the revolt as a series of "events" ([Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language "Hebrew language") מאורעות תרצ"ו-תרצ"ט) "riots", or "happenings".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003?_241-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwedenburg2003?-241">[229]</a></sup> The appropriate description was debated by Jewish Agency officials, who were keen not to give a negative impression of Palestine to prospective immigrants<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev1999433_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev1999433-242">[230]</a></sup> In private, however, [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") was unequivocal: the Arabs, he said, were "fighting dispossession ... The fear is not of losing land, but of losing the homeland of the Arab people, which others want to turn into the homeland of the Jewish people."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1999136_18-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1999136-18">[17]</a></sup>

British historian [Alan Allport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Allport "Alan Allport"), in his 2020 survey of the British Empire on the eve of the Second World War concludes that murderous incidents like al-Bassa:

> were outrageous precisely because they were unusual. On the whole, the British Army and the various colonial _gendarmeries_ that worked alongside it in the 1920s and 1930s behaved fairly well—certainly with a good deal more self-restraint than security forces of other imperial states. There is nothing in the British record in Palestine to compare with the devastating violence of the [Rif War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rif_War "Rif War") in Spanish Morocco for instance or the [Italian pacification of Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_colonization_of_Libya "Italian colonization of Libya"), both of which involve killing on a vastly greater scale. Many British soldiers behaved impeccably in Palestine during the Arab revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllport202051_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllport202051-243">[231]</a></sup>

He concludes that it was the "Palestine surge"—that is, London's use of sheer weight of numbers to overwhelm and crush the Arab rebels—was a success.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllport202066_244-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllport202066-244">[232]</a></sup>

Matthew Hughes, a leading authority on the Revolt, notes that it is a standard move in British historiography to contrast the relative mildness of British counter-insurgency achievements with those of other Western colonial powers. A contrast is frequently drawn between the [German suppression of the Herero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide "Herero and Namaqua genocide"), [Belgium's genocide in the Congo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State "Atrocities in the Congo Free State") and [France's violence in Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "Algerian War") to the winning-the-hearts-and-minds approach Britain is said to have adopted in Kenya in containing the [Mau Mau revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mau_Mau_rebellion "Mau Mau rebellion"). One British military commander asserted that 'If the Germans were in occupation in Haifa we'd not have any bloody troubles from the Arabs.'<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a314_245-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a314-245">[233]</a></sup> Nonetheless, while moderating forces did mitigate the violence, atrocities were committed, torture used, brutality commonplace. Collective punishment, the razing of villages, the smashing of personal property in homes, and the destruction of foodstocks was widespread. Britain's pacification succeeded and 'left Palestine in ruins.'<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a313–354_246-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2009a313%E2%80%93354-246">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes201915_247-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes201915-247">[235]</a></sup>

## Notes

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-16 "Jump up")** 'While the majority of Palestinian _fallāḥīn_ were dependent on bonds of "[patrimonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrimonialism "Patrimonialism") and elite parochialism" with notable families, these bonds weakened with urbanization as _a'yān_ (the Palestinian notable class) abetted, or were incapable of stopping, land sales and dispossessions.'<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanagan2013338_15-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanagan2013338-15">[15]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-29 "Jump up")** Hughes thinks this a conservative underestimate and calculates that a final figures might run from 5,748 to 7,272)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019381_28-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019381-28">[27]</a></sup>
3.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-72 "Jump up")** Laurens states that the identification is 'certain', citing [Yehoshua Porath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yehoshua_Porath "Yehoshua Porath").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPorath2015162_70-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPorath2015162-70">[68]</a></sup> Hughes states that this was denied by the Jewish press at the time:'The only basis for the suggestion that the assailants were Jews was apparently the fact that they were dressed in khaki shorts and jackets. It is submitted that this form of dress is not uncommon amongst the Arab workingmen of this particular neighbourhood.'<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes20192_71-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes20192-71">[69]</a></sup>
4.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-102 "Jump up")** "while the Zionist movement, after much agonising, accepted the principle of partition and the proposals as a basis for negotiation"; p. 49 "In the end, after bitter debate, the Congress equivocally approved – by a vote of 299 to 160 – the Peel recommendations as a basis for further negotiation."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris200411,_48–49_101-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris200411,_48%E2%80%9349-101">[98]</a></sup>
5.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-104 "Jump up")** "to negotiate a modified (Peel) proposal with the British." <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaiderSarnaZweig2012100_103-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaiderSarnaZweig2012100-103">[99]</a></sup>
6.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-106 "Jump up")** "The British government initially accepted the report in principle...With war clouds looming over Europe, they began to have second thoughts about the practicality of partition, fearing that to attempt to implement it against the will of the Palestinian Arab majority would rouse up the entire Arab world against Britain."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWasserstein2012339_105-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWasserstein2012339-105">[100]</a></sup>
7.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-171 "Jump up")** "it was the first manifestation of the Nashashibi group's armed defense against those who had violated the honor of their family and the honor of ... But when the general strike ended, he once again began coordinating his moves with the Zionists. The opposition's principal motivation for security cooperation was the assassination campaign pursued by the rebels at the behest of the Husseini leadership."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2009146_170-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2009146-170">[164]</a></sup>
8.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-196 "Jump up")** 'The contest of wills between the British Empire and the Palestinians was also an organizational battle for funds and equipment in which London would bankroll the Palestine Government and pay for the troops needed for pacification.'([Hughes 2019](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#CITEREFHughes2019), p. 82)
9.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-206 "Jump up")** Joseph Laniado, a Jewish Syrian parliamentarian told his Jewish contacts that Germany and Italy had channeled 'large amounts of money' to foment rebellion in Palestine’.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughes2019105–106_204-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughes2019105%E2%80%93106-204">[196]</a></sup> In June 1939, [Hans Piekenbrock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Piekenbrock "Hans Piekenbrock"), an intelligence colonel in the Abwehr's _Abteilung 1,_ boasted to his chief and friend [Admiral Canaris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Canaris "Wilhelm Canaris") that 'It was only as a result of the money we gave (al-Husayni) that it was possible to carry out the revolt in Palestine’.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerf200932_205-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerf200932-205">[197]</a></sup>
10.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-220 "Jump up")** The volume of Germany's funding was intentionally limited, as its goal was neither the collapse of the British Mandate nor the establishment of an independent Arab state (which would have been counterproductive to Germany's policy of expelling the Jews to Palestine), but to cause additional nuisance to the British.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364_207-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia1980364-207">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia201480–81_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia201480%E2%80%9381-219">[210]</a></sup>
11.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-231 "Jump up")** "the silencing of the opposition and humiliation of its leaders continued in the months that followed. In July 1938 an armed squad appeared at the home of a family of Nashashibi supporters in the village of Beit Rima, ...Before they left, the gang offered an explanation for their behavior: The jihad, they said, was directed against any person who did not obey the mufti. In the passion of the moment, they revealed the militants' fundamental tenet: Their national struggle was a religious holy war, and the incarnation of both the Palestinian Arab nation and Islam was Hajj Amin al-Husseini. Anyone who rejected his leadership was a heretic and his life was forfeit."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2009128_230-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2009128-230">[220]</a></sup>
12.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#cite_ref-235 "Jump up")** "Capping it all, the Permanent Mandates Commission of the Council of the League of Nations rejected the White Paper as inconsistent with the terms of the Mandate."([Morris 1999](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#CITEREFMorris1999), p. 159)
